class \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_d_g_m_r_e_s}{D\+G\+M\+R\+ES}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em A Restarted \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_g_m_r_e_s}{G\+M\+R\+ES}} with deflation. This class implements a modification of the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_g_m_r_e_s}{G\+M\+R\+ES}} solver for sparse linear systems. The basis is built with modified Gram-\/\+Schmidt. At each restart, a few approximated eigenvectors corresponding to the smallest eigenvalues are used to build a preconditioner for the next cycle. This preconditioner for deflation can be combined with any other preconditioner, the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_incomplete_l_u_t}{Incomplete\+L\+UT}} for instance. The preconditioner is applied at right of the matrix and the combination is multiplicative. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

class \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_i_d_r_s}{I\+D\+RS}}

class \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_i_d_r_s_t_a_b_l}{I\+D\+R\+S\+T\+A\+BL}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em The I\+D\+R(s)S\+T\+A\+B(l) is a combination of I\+D\+R(s) and Bi\+C\+G\+S\+T\+A\+B(l). It is a short-\/recurrences Krylov method for sparse square problems. It can outperform both I\+D\+R(s) and Bi\+C\+G\+S\+T\+A\+B(l). I\+D\+R(s)S\+T\+A\+B(l) generally closely follows the optimal \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_g_m_r_e_s}{G\+M\+R\+ES}} convergence in terms of the number of Matrix-\/\+Vector products. However, without the increasing cost per iteration of \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_g_m_r_e_s}{G\+M\+R\+ES}}. I\+D\+R(s)S\+T\+A\+B(l) is suitable for both indefinite systems and systems with complex eigenvalues. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef E\+I\+G\+E\+N\+\_\+\+D\+E\+F\+A\+U\+L\+T\+\_\+\+D\+E\+N\+S\+E\+\_\+\+I\+N\+D\+E\+X\+\_\+\+T\+Y\+PE \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Eigen\+::\+Index}}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EulerAxis}{EulerAxis}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361}{Eigen\+::\+Euler\+Axis}}}



Representation of a fixed signed rotation axis for \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_euler_system}{Euler\+System}}. 

Values here represent\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The axis of the rotation\+: X, Y or Z.
\item The sign (i.\+e. direction of the rotation along the axis)\+: positive(+) or negative(-\/)
\end{DoxyItemize}

Therefore, this could express all the axes \{+X,+Y,+Z,-\/X,-\/Y,-\/Z\}

For positive axis, use +E\+U\+L\+E\+R\+\_\+\{axis\}, and for negative axis use -\/E\+U\+L\+E\+R\+\_\+\{axis\}. \begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{EULER\_X@{EULER\_X}!Eigen@{Eigen}}\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!EULER\_X@{EULER\_X}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361ae8110af93d433bfcf247d6bac5e1d387}\label{namespace_eigen_ae614aa7cdd687fb5c421a54f2ce5c361ae8110af93d433bfcf247d6bac5e1d387}} 
E\+U\+L\+E\+R\+\_\+X&the X axis \\
\hline

\doxysubsection{Function Documentation}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_ae29347f850e265d2d33164b3387ba360}\label{namespace_eigen_ae29347f850e265d2d33164b3387ba360}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!accurateDot@{accurateDot}}
\index{accurateDot@{accurateDot}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{accurateDot()}{accurateDot()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Derived , typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
Derived\+::\+Scalar Eigen\+::accurate\+Dot (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_sparse_matrix_base}{Sparse\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$ \&}]{A,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_sparse_matrix_base}{Sparse\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



computes an accurate dot product on two sparse vectors 

Uses an accurate summation algorithm for the accumulator in order to compute an accurate dot product for two sparse vectors. \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_afdf5abdb29bfceb4625e62e35c830ce4}\label{namespace_eigen_afdf5abdb29bfceb4625e62e35c830ce4}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!bessel\_i0@{bessel\_i0}}
\index{bessel\_i0@{bessel\_i0}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{bessel\_i0()}{bessel\_i0()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
const E\+I\+G\+E\+N\+\_\+\+S\+T\+R\+O\+N\+G\+\_\+\+I\+N\+L\+I\+NE \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_cwise_unary_op}{Eigen\+::\+Cwise\+Unary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__bessel__i0__op}{Eigen\+::internal\+::scalar\+\_\+bessel\+\_\+i0\+\_\+op}}$<$ typename Derived\+::\+Scalar $>$, const Derived $>$ Eigen\+::bessel\+\_\+i0 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$ \&}]{x }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise i0({\itshape x}) to the given arrays.
\end{DoxyReturn}
It returns the modified Bessel function of the first kind of order zero.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em x} & is the argument\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function supports only float and double scalar types. To support other scalar types, the user has to provide implementations of i0(\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Array\+Base\+::bessel\+\_\+i0() 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_ae5e6995d520140092109482a34c21cac}\label{namespace_eigen_ae5e6995d520140092109482a34c21cac}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!bessel\_i0e@{bessel\_i0e}}
\index{bessel\_i0e@{bessel\_i0e}!Eigen@{Eigen}}

This function computes the regularized incomplete beta function (integral). \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a21a251a5c15e1eebb3f03633f4945c74}\label{namespace_eigen_a21a251a5c15e1eebb3f03633f4945c74}}

\index{betainc@{betainc}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{betainc()}{betainc()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Arg\+A\+Derived , typename Arg\+B\+Derived , typename Arg\+X\+Derived $>$ \\
const E\+I\+G\+E\+N\+\_\+\+S\+T\+R\+O\+N\+G\+\_\+\+I\+N\+L\+I\+NE \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_cwise_ternary_op}{Eigen\+::\+Cwise\+Ternary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__betainc__op}{Eigen\+::internal\+::scalar\+\_\+betainc\+\_\+op}}$<$ typename Arg\+X\+Derived\+::\+Scalar $>$, const Arg\+A\+Derived, const Arg\+B\+Derived, const Arg\+X\+Derived $>$ Eigen\+::betainc (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Arg\+A\+Derived $>$ \&}]{a,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Arg\+B\+Derived $>$ \&}]{b,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Arg\+X\+Derived $>$ \&}]{x }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\textbackslash{}cpp11 \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise betainc({\itshape x}, {\itshape a}, {\itshape b}) to the given arrays.
\end{DoxyReturn}
This function computes the regularized incomplete beta function (integral).

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function supports only float and double scalar types in c++11 mode. To support other scalar types, or float/double in non c++11 mode, the user has to provide implementations of betainc(\+T,\+T,\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}

\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!BVIntersect@{BVIntersect}}
\index{BVIntersect@{BVIntersect}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{BVIntersect()}{BVIntersect()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename B\+VH , typename Intersector $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::\+B\+V\+Intersect (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const B\+VH \&}]{tree,  }\item[{Intersector \&}]{intersector }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Given a B\+VH, runs the query encapsulated by {\itshape intersector}. The Intersector type must provide the following members\+:
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{bool} intersectVolume(\textcolor{keyword}{const} BVH::Volume \&volume) \textcolor{comment}{//returns true if volume intersects the query}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{bool} intersectObject(\textcolor{keyword}{const} BVH::Object \&\textcolor{keywordtype}{object}) \textcolor{comment}{//returns true if the search should terminate immediately}}
\end{DoxyCode}
 \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_ac3b8047a3ee05b5e6fec4668197a9a43}\label{namespace_eigen_ac3b8047a3ee05b5e6fec4668197a9a43}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!BVIntersect@{BVIntersect}}
\index{BVIntersect@{BVIntersect}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{BVIntersect()}{BVIntersect()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{createRandomPIMatrixOfRank()}{createRandomPIMatrixOfRank()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Matrix\+Type $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::create\+Random\+P\+I\+Matrix\+Of\+Rank (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{desired\+\_\+rank,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{rows,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{cols,  }\item[{Matrix\+Type \&}]{m }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Creates a random partial isometry matrix of given rank.

A partial isometry is a matrix all of whose singular values are either 0 or 1. This is very useful to test rank-\/revealing algorithms.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Matrix\+Type} & type of random partial isometry matrix \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\hline
{\em cols} & column dimension of requested random partial isometry matrix \\
\hline
{\em m} & random partial isometry matrix \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_af9581b8fef58e77009b9c07137d8fa4d}\label{namespace_eigen_af9581b8fef58e77009b9c07137d8fa4d}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!generateRandomMatrixSvs@{generateRandomMatrixSvs}}
\index{generateRandomMatrixSvs@{generateRandomMatrixSvs}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{generateRandomMatrixSvs()}{generateRandomMatrixSvs()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Matrix\+Type , typename Real\+Scalar\+Vector\+Type $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::generate\+Random\+Matrix\+Svs (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Real\+Scalar\+Vector\+Type \&}]{svs,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{rows,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{cols,  }\item[{Matrix\+Type \&}]{M }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Generation of random matrix with prescribed singular values.

We generate random matrices with given singular values by setting up a singular value decomposition. By choosing the number of zeros as singular values we can specify the rank of the matrix. Moreover, we also control its spectral norm, which is the largest singular value, as well as its condition number with respect to the l2-\/norm, which is the quotient of the largest and smallest singular value.

Reference\+: For details on the method see e.\+g. Section 8.\+1 (pp. 62 f) in

C. C. Paige, M. A. Saunders, L\+S\+QR\+: An algorithm for sparse linear equations and sparse least squares. A\+CM Transactions on Mathematical Software 8(1), pp. 43-\/71, 1982. \href{https://web.stanford.edu/group/SOL/software/lsqr/lsqr-toms82a.pdf}{\texttt{ https\+://web.\+stanford.\+edu/group/\+S\+O\+L/software/lsqr/lsqr-\/toms82a.\+pdf}}

and also the L\+S\+QR webpage \href{https://web.stanford.edu/group/SOL/software/lsqr/}{\texttt{ https\+://web.\+stanford.\+edu/group/\+S\+O\+L/software/lsqr/}}.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Matrix\+Type} & matrix type to generate \\
\hline
{\em Real\+Scalar\+Vector\+Type} & vector type with real entries used for singular values \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em svs} & vector of desired singular values \\
\hline
{\em rows} & row dimension of requested random matrix \\
\hline
{\em cols} & column dimension of requested random matrix \\
\hline
{\em M} & generated matrix with prescribed singular values \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_ac33a0d76d99d352dd36cf73987d8eca7}\label{namespace_eigen_ac33a0d76d99d352dd36cf73987d8eca7}}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_ad6d0ed07a6ee97fcef4fe3bce6a674d4}\label{namespace_eigen_ad6d0ed07a6ee97fcef4fe3bce6a674d4}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!klu\_solve@{klu\_solve}}
\index{klu\_solve@{klu\_solve}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{klu\_solve()}{klu\_solve()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily int Eigen\+::klu\+\_\+solve (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{klu\+\_\+symbolic $\ast$}]{Symbolic,  }\item[{klu\+\_\+numeric $\ast$}]{Numeric,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{ldim,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{nrhs,  }\item[{double}]{B\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]},  }\item[{klu\+\_\+common $\ast$}]{Common,  }\item[{double}]{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



A sparse LU factorization and solver based on \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_k_l_u}{K\+LU}}. 

This class allows to solve for A.\+X = B sparse linear problems via a LU factorization using the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_k_l_u}{K\+LU}} library. The sparse matrix A must be squared and full rank. The vectors or matrices X and B can be either dense or sparse.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
The input matrix A should be in a {\bfseries{compressed}} and {\bfseries{column-\/major}} form. Otherwise an expensive copy will be made. You can call the inexpensive make\+Compressed() to get a compressed matrix. 
\end{DoxyWarning}

\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Matrix\+Type\+\_\+} & the type of the sparse matrix A, it must be a Sparse\+Matrix$<$$>$\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
\textbackslash{}implsparsesolverconcept

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\mbox{\hyperlink{SparseLinearSystems.dox_TutorialSparseSolverConcept}{Sparse solver concept}}, class \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_umf_pack_l_u}{Umf\+Pack\+LU}}, class \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_sparse_l_u}{Sparse\+LU}} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a4e6cd3acfea39bcff3fa38e0de1226f5}\label{namespace_eigen_a4e6cd3acfea39bcff3fa38e0de1226f5}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!kroneckerProduct@{kroneckerProduct}}
\index{kroneckerProduct@{kroneckerProduct}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kroneckerProduct()}{kroneckerProduct()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename A , typename B $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_kronecker_product_sparse}{Kronecker\+Product\+Sparse}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{A}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{B}} $>$ Eigen\+::kronecker\+Product (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1_eigen_base}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{A}} $>$ \&}]{a,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1_eigen_base}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{B}} $>$ \&}]{b }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Computes Kronecker tensor product of two matrices, at least one of which is sparse

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If you want to replace a matrix by its Kronecker product with some matrix, do {\bfseries{N\+OT}} do this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A = \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}{kroneckerProduct}}(A,\mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{B}}); \textcolor{comment}{// bug!!! caused by aliasing effect}}
\end{DoxyCode}
 instead, use eval() to work around this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A = \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}{kroneckerProduct}}(A,\mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{B}}).eval();}
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyWarning}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em a} & Dense/sparse matrix a \\
\hline
{\em b} & Dense/sparse matrix b \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Kronecker tensor product of a and b, stored in a sparse matrix 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}\label{namespace_eigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!kroneckerProduct@{kroneckerProduct}}
\index{kroneckerProduct@{kroneckerProduct}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kroneckerProduct()}{kroneckerProduct()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename A , typename B $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_kronecker_product}{Kronecker\+Product}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{A}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{B}} $>$ Eigen\+::kronecker\+Product (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix_base}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{A}} $>$ \&}]{a,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix_base}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{B}} $>$ \&}]{b }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Computes Kronecker tensor product of two dense matrices

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If you want to replace a matrix by its Kronecker product with some matrix, do {\bfseries{N\+OT}} do this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A = \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}{kroneckerProduct}}(A,\mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{B}}); \textcolor{comment}{// bug!!! caused by aliasing effect}}
\end{DoxyCode}
 instead, use eval() to work around this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A = \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_aedd4b7cd1e324ed0769cac2701f4d050}{kroneckerProduct}}(A,\mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{B}}).eval();}
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyWarning}

\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

Kronecker tensor product of a and b 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular@{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular}}
\index{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular@{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular()}{matrix\_sqrt\_quasi\_triangular()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Matrix\+Type , typename Result\+Type $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::matrix\+\_\+sqrt\+\_\+quasi\+\_\+triangular (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Matrix\+Type \&}]{arg,  }\item[{Result\+Type \&}]{result }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute matrix square root of quasi-\/triangular matrix. 


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Matrix\+Type} & type of {\ttfamily arg}, the argument of matrix square root, expected to be an instantiation of the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} class template. \\
\hline
{\em Result\+Type} & type of {\ttfamily result}, where result is to be stored. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em arg} & argument of matrix square root. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em result} & matrix square root of upper Hessenberg part of {\ttfamily arg}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function computes the square root of the upper quasi-\/triangular matrix stored in the upper Hessenberg part of {\ttfamily arg}. Only the upper Hessenberg part of {\ttfamily result} is updated, the rest is not touched. See \mbox{\hyperlink{group__core__func__exponential_ga5c784ec51a1765be0a623104db2577b6}{Matrix\+Base\+::sqrt()}} for details on how this computation is implemented.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Matrix\+Square\+Root, Matrix\+Square\+Root\+Quasi\+Triangular 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_ae51c91f920f6ea4a7f6f72caa1e8249f}\label{namespace_eigen_ae51c91f920f6ea4a7f6f72caa1e8249f}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!matrix\_sqrt\_triangular@{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular}}
\index{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular@{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular()}{matrix\_sqrt\_triangular()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Matrix\+Type , typename Result\+Type $>$ \\
void Eigen\+::matrix\+\_\+sqrt\+\_\+triangular (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Matrix\+Type \&}]{arg,  }\item[{Result\+Type \&}]{result }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute matrix square root of triangular matrix. 


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Matrix\+Type} & type of {\ttfamily arg}, the argument of matrix square root, expected to be an instantiation of the \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} class template. \\
\hline
{\em Result\+Type} & type of {\ttfamily result}, where result is to be stored. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em arg} & argument of matrix square root. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em result} & matrix square root of upper triangular part of {\ttfamily arg}.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Only the upper triangular part (including the diagonal) of {\ttfamily result} is updated, the rest is not touched. See \mbox{\hyperlink{group__core__func__exponential_ga5c784ec51a1765be0a623104db2577b6}{Matrix\+Base\+::sqrt()}} for details on how this computation is implemented.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{operator$\ast$@{operator$\ast$}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operator$\ast$()}{operator*()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [4/9]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Other\+Derived , typename Vectors\+Type , typename Coeffs\+Type , int Side$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1internal_1_1matrix__type__times__scalar__type}{internal\+::matrix\+\_\+type\+\_\+times\+\_\+scalar\+\_\+type}}$<$ typename Vectors\+Type\+::\+Scalar, Other\+Derived $>$\+::Type Eigen\+::operator$\ast$ (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix_base}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_householder_sequence}{Householder\+Sequence}}$<$ Vectors\+Type, Coeffs\+Type, Side $>$ \&}]{h }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the product of a matrix with a Householder sequence. 


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em other} & Matrix being multiplied. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em h} & Householder\+Sequence being multiplied. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Expression object representing the product.
\end{DoxyReturn}
This function computes $ MH $ where $ M $ is the matrix {\ttfamily other} and $ H $ is the Householder sequence represented by {\ttfamily h}. \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a9c2c1af8da495ae3cbe7be12cecfe294}\label{namespace_eigen_a9c2c1af8da495ae3cbe7be12cecfe294}}

\index{operator$\ast$@{operator$\ast$}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operator$\ast$()}{operator*()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [5/9]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Sparse\+Derived , typename Perm\+Derived $>$ \\

\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!polygamma@{polygamma}}
\index{polygamma@{polygamma}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{polygamma()}{polygamma()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename DerivedN , typename DerivedX $>$ \\
const E\+I\+G\+E\+N\+\_\+\+S\+T\+R\+O\+N\+G\+\_\+\+I\+N\+L\+I\+NE \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_cwise_binary_op}{Eigen\+::\+Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__polygamma__op}{Eigen\+::internal\+::scalar\+\_\+polygamma\+\_\+op}}$<$ typename Derived\+X\+::\+Scalar $>$, const DerivedN, const DerivedX $>$ Eigen\+::polygamma (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ DerivedN $>$ \&}]{n,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ DerivedX $>$ \&}]{x }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\textbackslash{}cpp11 \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise polygamma({\itshape n}, {\itshape x}) to the given arrays.
\end{DoxyReturn}
It returns the {\itshape n} -\/th derivative of the digamma(psi) evaluated at {\ttfamily x}.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function supports only float and double scalar types in c++11 mode. To support other scalar types, or float/double in non c++11 mode, the user has to provide implementations of polygamma(\+T,\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Eigen\+::digamma() 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

Given the roots of a polynomial compute the coefficients in the monomial basis of the monic polynomial with same roots and minimal degree. If Root\+Vector is a vector of complexes, Polynomial should also be a vector of complexes.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a1fb05f2dfd1e1974dc016cff6f349f98}\label{namespace_eigen_a1fb05f2dfd1e1974dc016cff6f349f98}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!run@{run}}
\index{run@{run}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{run()}{run()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Kernel , typename... Args$>$ \\
auto Eigen\+::run (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Kernel}]{kernel,  }\item[{Args \&\&...}]{args }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) -\/$>$ decltype(kernel(args...))}

Runs a kernel on the G\+PU (if E\+I\+G\+E\+N\+\_\+\+G\+P\+U\+CC), or C\+PU otherwise.

This is to better support creating generic tests.

The kernel must be able to be passed directly as an input to a global function (i.\+e. empty or P\+OD). Its inputs must be \char`\"{}\+Serializable\char`\"{} so we can transfer them to the device, and the output must be a Serializable value type so it can be transferred back from the device.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em kernel} & kernel to run. \\
\hline
{\em args} & ... input arguments, must be \char`\"{}\+Serializable\char`\"{}. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
kernel(args...). 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a363009311edea9cf1cb642b946518cbc}\label{namespace_eigen_a363009311edea9cf1cb642b946518cbc}}

\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!run\_with\_hint@{run\_with\_hint}}
\index{run\_with\_hint@{run\_with\_hint}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{run\_with\_hint()}{run\_with\_hint()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Kernel , typename... Args$>$ \\
auto Eigen\+::run\+\_\+with\+\_\+hint (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{buffer\+\_\+capacity\+\_\+hint,  }\item[{Kernel}]{kernel,  }\item[{Args \&\&...}]{args }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) -\/$>$ decltype(kernel(args...))}

Runs a kernel on the G\+PU (if E\+I\+G\+E\+N\+\_\+\+G\+P\+U\+CC), or C\+PU otherwise.

This version allows specifying a minimum buffer capacity size required for serializing the puts to transfer results from device to host. Use this when {\ttfamily run(...)} fails to determine an appropriate capacity by default.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\hline
{\em kernel} & kernel to run. \\
\hline

\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

kernel(args...). 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setupRandomSvs()}{setupRandomSvs()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Vector\+Type , typename Real\+Scalar $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_vector_type}{Vector\+Type}} Eigen\+::setup\+Random\+Svs (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{dim,  }\item[{const Real\+Scalar}]{max }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Setup a vector of random singular values with prescribed upper limit. For use with \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_af9581b8fef58e77009b9c07137d8fa4d}{generate\+Random\+Matrix\+Svs()}}.

Singular values are non-\/negative real values. By convention (to be consistent with singular value decomposition) we sort them in decreasing order.

This strategy produces random singular values in the range \mbox{[}0, max\mbox{]}, in particular the singular values can be zero or arbitrarily close to zero.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_vector_type}{Vector\+Type}}} & vector type with real entries used for singular values \\
\hline
{\em Real\+Scalar} & data type used for real entry \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em dim} & number of singular values to generate \\
\hline
{\em max} & upper bound for singular values \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
vector of singular values 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!setupRangeSvs@{setupRangeSvs}}
\index{setupRangeSvs@{setupRangeSvs}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setupRangeSvs()}{setupRangeSvs()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename Vector\+Type , typename Real\+Scalar $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_vector_type}{Vector\+Type}} Eigen\+::setup\+Range\+Svs (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{dim,  }\item[{const Real\+Scalar}]{min,  }\item[{const Real\+Scalar}]{max }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Setup a vector of random singular values with prescribed range. For use with \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_eigen_af9581b8fef58e77009b9c07137d8fa4d}{generate\+Random\+Matrix\+Svs()}}.

Singular values are non-\/negative real values. By convention (to be consistent with singular value decomposition) we sort them in decreasing order.

For dim $>$ 1 this strategy generates a vector with largest entry max, smallest entry min, and remaining entries in the range \mbox{[}min, max\mbox{]}. For dim == 1 the only entry is min.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_vector_type}{Vector\+Type}}} & vector type with real entries used for singular values \\

\hline
{\em max} & largest singular value to use \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

vector of singular values

const E\+I\+G\+E\+N\+\_\+\+S\+T\+R\+O\+N\+G\+\_\+\+I\+N\+L\+I\+NE \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_cwise_binary_op}{Eigen\+::\+Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__zeta__op}{Eigen\+::internal\+::scalar\+\_\+zeta\+\_\+op}}$<$ typename Derived\+X\+::\+Scalar $>$, const DerivedX, const DerivedQ $>$ Eigen\+::zeta (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ DerivedX $>$ \&}]{x,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ DerivedQ $>$ \&}]{q }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

It returns the Riemann zeta function of two arguments {\itshape x} and {\itshape q\+:} 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\doxysubsection{Variable Documentation}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_ad81fa7195215a0ce30017dfac309f0b2}\label{namespace_eigen_ad81fa7195215a0ce30017dfac309f0b2}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!Dynamic@{Dynamic}}
\index{Dynamic@{Dynamic}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Dynamic}{Dynamic}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const int Eigen\+::\+Dynamic = -\/1}

This value means that a positive quantity (e.\+g., a size) is not known at compile-\/time, and that instead the value is stored in some runtime variable.

Changing the value of Dynamic breaks the A\+BI, as Dynamic is often used as a template parameter for \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}. \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a73c597189a4a99127175e8167c456fff}\label{namespace_eigen_a73c597189a4a99127175e8167c456fff}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!DynamicIndex@{DynamicIndex}}
\index{DynamicIndex@{DynamicIndex}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DynamicIndex}{DynamicIndex}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const int Eigen\+::\+Dynamic\+Index = 0xffffff}

This value means that a signed quantity (e.\+g., a signed index) is not known at compile-\/time, and that instead its value has to be specified at runtime. \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_aad94bff6c8d08a5edaf5a39694e5345e}\label{namespace_eigen_aad94bff6c8d08a5edaf5a39694e5345e}}

\end{DoxyCode}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a3163430a1c13173faffde69016b48aaf}\label{namespace_eigen_a3163430a1c13173faffde69016b48aaf}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!HugeCost@{HugeCost}}
\index{HugeCost@{HugeCost}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{HugeCost}{HugeCost}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const int Eigen\+::\+Huge\+Cost = 10000}

This value means that the cost to evaluate an expression coefficient is either very expensive or cannot be known at compile time.

This value has to be positive to (1) simplify cost computation, and (2) allow to distinguish between a very expensive and very very expensive expressions. It thus must also be large enough to make sure unrolling won\textquotesingle{}t happen and that sub expressions will be evaluated, but not too large to avoid overflow. \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a7951593b031e13d90223c83d022ce99e}\label{namespace_eigen_a7951593b031e13d90223c83d022ce99e}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!Infinity@{Infinity}}
\index{Infinity@{Infinity}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Infinity}{Infinity}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const int Eigen\+::\+Infinity = -\/1}

This value means +Infinity; it is currently used only as the p parameter to Matrix\+Base\+::lp\+Norm$<$int$>$(). The value Infinity there means the L-\/infinity norm. \mbox{\Hypertarget{namespace_eigen_a06808a853a9baa38b23a5368e7491abd}\label{namespace_eigen_a06808a853a9baa38b23a5368e7491abd}} 
\index{Eigen@{Eigen}!UndefinedIncr@{UndefinedIncr}}
\index{UndefinedIncr@{UndefinedIncr}!Eigen@{Eigen}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UndefinedIncr}{UndefinedIncr}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const int Eigen\+::\+Undefined\+Incr = 0xfffffe}

This value means that the increment to go from one value to another in a sequence is not constant for each step.
